I'm on a (small) mission to stop saying "I don't know". I use it as a filler and I really dislike it when my conversation is filled with empty fillers. I'd rather say nothing at all! And maybe that's why I'm more quiet than talkative. It's crossed my mind as something I should stop using as a crutch and now that I'm proclaiming it here on my IG I guess I'm going to have to really stick to it! ğŸ˜ I found that I was not taking responsibility or really articulating my thoughts whenever I used that phrase. Now that I'm eliminating it, I pause before I speak and fill it with something substantial. I don't know, I'll let you know how it goes .... Ray Caesarâ€˜s ( @raycaesar1111 ) portraits frequently involve childlike creatures with physical deformities and grotesque elements set against a fairy tale backdrop of darkness and sexual innuendos. He was one of Empty Kingdomâ€™s Top 100 artists in 2012 and was featured regularly in the past.
#emptykingdom #ekart #painting #surreal #london #raycaesar
Mark Ryden ( @markryden ) created a singular style that blurs the traditional boundaries between high and low art. His work first garnered attention in the 1990s when he ushered in a new genre of painting, "Pop Surrealism", dragging a host of followers in his wake. Ryden has trumped the initial surrealist strategies by choosing subject matter loaded with cultural connotation. #emptykingdom #ekart #painting #popsurrealism #losangeles #markryden

Island Lore:

A campfire story, I told him about the Nicollet Island Bigfoot. My son, his imagination billows larger than his small frame can support. It was a story in jest- a flicker, a passing moment of yetis and choose your own adventure, and things in the night. It reminds me, he believes. I do too, and you too, we all believe in stories and imagination and adventure. And so I hold him tight, his small stature with his full heart and body filled with wonder.

#nicolletisland

Another great filming day on the mountains of Dovrefjell. Today, after a long hike, we made a snow cave. It's the sheer joy of creating something new from a scratch - with the way of the nature. Looking forward to spending the night in our new winter apartment. 
#katoavapohjola @oppdalsafari @yletv1 #conservation #savethearctic #documentary #kimmoohtonen  #finland #norway #savetheplanet #dovrefjell #yle
Greetings from the Dovrefjell National Park in Norway. Today we started filming the last episode of the six part documentary series that I've been working on for the past year and half. The series explores the relationship between man and the Nordic nature - and tries to find answers on what the future looks like for people and nature in the Nordic part of the world. The series will be shown from November onwards in, at least, Finland, France and Denmark. 
My mission in the last episode is to explore (first in Norway, then in Greenland) how the tumultuous changes to our globe, such as the climate change, are affecting the Nordic nature. 
I've got a feeling this is going to be another memorable trip on the snowy mountains of Dovrefjell. 
#katoavapohjola #documentary #climatechange #savetheplanet #savethearctic #yle #finland @yleisradio @yletv1 #kimmoohtonen #conservation #arte #dr

Part II of vintage lens meets modern camera.  The Nikon 105 f2.5 proved to be a killer combo. Sharpness for days and beautiful color rendition. More info and photos on our blog found on AcmeCameraRental.com.  #nikkorlens #nikkor105mm25 #nikon105mm #nikkor #nikon #nikonlove #nikonphotography #portrait #portraiture
So it turns out that Old lenses+New cameras= freakin' awesome!  We took some time out today to photograph @madeleineme with our Nikon D7100 and a 40 year old Nikon 105mm f2.5 lens. We were amazed by the sharpness and beautiful color this combination can produce. Heck we were so excited we went ahead and wrote a blog article about it. We'll share a few more photos later but you should jump over to our site and check out the article sometime.  We'd love it if you did.  #nikon #nikonvintage #vintageglass #d7100 #nikon105mm  #nikkor #nikkor105mm25 #ã«ã£ã“ã‚Š #nikkorlens #nikonlove

A family that we met on our trip through Sri Lanka invited us for a lunch. They treated us with great hospitality and kindness. CALL FOR SUBMISSIONS.â€¢*â€¢~ âœ¨ I Can Be My Own Muse Now zine âœ¨ i am interested in opening a discussion about feminist culture on the Internet ~ how self portraiture (specifically through photography) in the digital world has created a space for connection, how it has enabled us to support/encourage both ourselves as well as each other through communicating self love/self exploration/growth and how this conversation translates into the physical world. with this project i would like to primarily focus on self portraits in which our physical selves are present in the space of the image. if you are interested in contributing please send me your photographs (film & digital & iphone all welcome) and a few words about what it means to you .â€¢*â€¢to be your own muse.â€¢~ feel free to send as many as you like, high-res files! please include your name & age. deadline is FEBRUARY 1 ğŸ“¬ send all submissions to littlesunlady@gmail.com ğŸ“¬ - @littlesunlady

Vegan UFC Fighter Nate Diaz stepped in to fight the formidable Conor McGregor on only 12 days notice and claimed a shock victory after beating his opponent in the second round. McGregor was unable to keep up with Diaz and was completely overwhelmed by Diaz's energy and unrelenting pace .

McGregor, who was previously unbeaten in UFC, was caught by a powerful left hand in the second round which stunned the UFC featherweight champion - fighting for the first time at welterweight 25 lbs heavier - and Diaz simply took his opportunity and poured on the pressure .

Diaz took McGregor to the ground and the fight was his. The Brazilian Jiu-Jitsu black belt finished the fight quickly after McGregor was forced to submit .

Nate, has been a strict vegan since he was 18 years, following the advice of his older brother Nick, who is also a UFC fighter. They mostly consume a raw plant-based diet and credit this with their superior performance capabilities. Both brothers have incredible cardio, compete in triathlons and never seem to fade for a second in fights despite pushing a frantic pace ğŸ™ŒğŸ¼ğŸ™ğŸ¼ğŸ™ŒğŸ¼ #consciousbeardman#vegan#fighter#muaythai#mma#bjj#ufc#diazbrothers#noirishluckhere#AnonNova#peacefulwarrior#natediaz#nickdiaz#therealchamp #vegantakeover #veganpower

ğŸ¸How To: Get Rid Of PimplesğŸ¸
ğŸ’ğŸ»Make a cucumber mask. This solution works best for soothing your skin and reducing redness, but is not as effective as aforementioned solutions for killing bacteria. Mince a bit of cucumber to form a paste, and put this directly on your pimple or over your whole face. Wait for it to set for 15-20 minutes, and then rinse your skin off with cold water. Voila! Your redness should be significantly reduced, and youâ€™ll feel cool as a cucumber.
ğŸ’¦Keep your skin clean. Throughout the day, pollution from the air, sweat, and dirt stick to the skin on your face and make your pimples worse. Wash your face twice daily, and keep cleansing pads/towelettes with you throughout the day. This way, whenever your face feels oily, grimy, or sweaty, you can wipe it off and leave your skin fresh and clean. These are especially handy for after a workout and in hot weather.
ğŸ‹Another quick way to get rid of pimples is the use of lemon juice, which is rich in vitamin C. Lemon juice helps pimples dry up faster. Be sure to use fresh lemon juice and not bottled juice, which has preservatives. There are a couple of ways to apply this remedy. Dip a clean cotton swab in fresh lemon juice and apply it to the pimples before going to bed.
You can also mix one tablespoon of lemon juice with one teaspoon of cinnamon powder and put it on the pimples overnight. In the morning, wash the skin well with lukewarm water. However, this particular remedy is not suitable for those with sensitive skin.

Here's a little before and after photo to show you guys my skin progression, and also because a lot of you guys have asked what I've done which has helped my skin so much! You can't really tell how bad my skin was in my before photos, it was so much more red and inflamed than it looks- I never ever felt confident about my skin, not even wearing makeup because it was still covered in huge painful lumps. The main thing I can put my skin improvements down to is my choice of makeup- I used to wear whatever foundation I felt like wearing, liquid maybelene, revlon, cover girl, anything that would give me the most coverage, I would literally drown my foundation until you wouldn't see a hint of redness, I would even go to the gym with makeup on. Then my skin specialist recommended I switch to natural, mineral powder rather than liquid foundation. That, paired with using @dermaviduals skin care products I was prescribed from @house.of.maxx in Melbourne, really helped my skin. It was really gradual, I first started seeing my skin specialist in Sydney last June, and I've only really noticed a huge improvement in my skin in the last two or so months. 
What has worked for me may not necessarily work for everyone, but if you're having skin troubles, at least try to switch your makeup and see if that helps! If you've got sensitive skin like me, you need to be incredibly picky about what you put on your face, and normal supermarket makeup will do major damage to your skin! That plus taking vitamins like Zinc, fish oil, and specific skin vitamins like vitex are amazing too! Don't give up hope, bad skin doesn't last forever. Yes it makes you feel like absolute crap, but it will get better. Just keep trying different things, and eventually you will find something that works for you!

Well, damn. I managed to avoid the most classic injury for female skiers--a blown ACL--until my 11th year on tour (I went big and tore my MCL right off tooğŸ™„). I'm so so bummed to end my season short as I was making progress every day, feeling so great on my skis, and hadn't quite finished my previous comeback. But, I'm also so so thankful that I didn't hit my head again. Compared to brains, injuring knees feels like a luxury because a doctor can actually fix them, tell you exactly how to get better, and when you'll be able to get back to sport. It's all about perspective. Thank you to everyone for your support and to Dr. Heard for being the best surgeon/human being out there! As of yesterday, Fujifilm decided to discontinue the last of the film that I have been exclusively using this year. What's left on the Internet and in stores is all that there is. It's unfortunate to see such an amazing film vanish and render thousands of cameras entirely useless. In the next few weeks I will be on a mission to find as much of this film as I can so I can continue to work on the book that I have been piecing together shot entirely on the Fujifilm FP-100c. Itâ€™s easy to equate success with luck, but that is often not the case, and those that are seemingly lucky have put in the hard work to get that way. Luck has been described as the moment when preparation meets opportunity, so you have to put in the work to get prepared for the time when opportunity comes knocking. You may have opportunities presented to you but you are not prepared to capitalize on them, and therefore cannot take advantage of that lucky moment. Put in the work and the opportunities will come and youâ€™ll be ready for them.

I hold in my hands one of the most toxic substances of the century. This substance affects you whether or not you consume genetically modified organisms. 
In the longest study performed on GMOs and #Roundup (2-years) conclusive data was achieved proving the harmful and toxic affects on the liver and kidneys.

Then there's the cancer causing aspect. The number of large tumors the rats they studied developed was unbelievable. The World Health Organization has classified  glyphosate (the "perceived" active ingredient) as a category 2A carcinogen. 
Yesterday I brought the researcher and toxicologist from this study on my @fox5sandiego #foodasmedicine show with me. 
Professor Seralini came all the way from France to share the groundbreaking research of his 3.2 million dollar, 2-year study. He found shocking data about how #glyphosate is actually the lessor of the evils when it comes to the other hidden chemicals in the product.

GMOs and toxic herbicides have increased exponentially over the past 10 years. They are using glyphosate not only in #GMOs but also on lawns, in parks, schools, and golf courses. And many people still don't know better and even use it in their own garden. It's also used as a drying agent in #nongmo foods like lentils and oats. 
This study paves the way for us to vote to stop the use altogether until more epidemiological studies have been performed. 
The link to this show and a transcript to my 20-minute follow up interview with the professor is in my profile. This man has sacrificed his whole life and reputation for this cause. He's recently won three lawsuits for defamation caused by #Monsanto. He is a hero of our time and is to be celebrated. 
Now I want to hear your thoughts below... and please tag your friends who need to know this. 
In case you're wondering, yes, I immediately returned this toxic shit right after the segment ;) #nongmoproject

Happy birthday to my son who would be 9 years old todayğŸˆHe is the inspiration behind my sanctuary & the reason that I was able to fully #maketheconnection I had gone back & forth with vegetarianism for years but after the passing of my son, I saw footage of a mother cow experiencing the same agonizing grief when they stole her calf from her. She collapsed in the mud, wailing for her baby.. just as I did that rainy day. They were putting her through this so that humans can steal her breast milk. Breast milk that is naturally intended for her baby. It hit me like a ton of bricks. Animals love their young & they mourn their loss, just as humans do. All mothers love their babies, no matter the species. The meat & dairy industry makes bereaved mothers of millions over & over again. Please join me in stopping this. Don't contribute to this heartbreaking cruelty! Thank you to my son Danny for opening my eyes & my heart to the truth. I love you & I miss you every minute of everyday. #govegan

Current models of visual perception typically assume that human vision estimates true properties of physical objects, properties that exist even if unperceived. However, recent studies of perceptual evolution, using evolutionary games and genetic algorithms, reveal that natural selection often drives true perceptions to extinction when they compete with perceptions tuned to fitness rather than truth: Perception guides adaptive behavior; it does not estimate a preexisting physical truth. Moreover, shifting from evolutionary biology to quantum physics, there is reason to disbelieve in preexisting physical truths: Certain interpretations of quantum theory deny that dynamical properties of physical objects have definite values when unobserved. In some of these interpretations the observer is fundamental, and wave functions are compendia of subjective probabilities, not preexisting elements of physical reality. These two considerations, from evolutionary biology and quantum physics, suggest that current models of object perception require fundamental reformulation. Here we begin such a reformulation, starting with a formal model of consciousness that we call a â€œconscious agent.â€ We develop the dynamics of interacting conscious agents, and study how the perception of objects and space-time can emerge from such dynamics. We show that one particular object, the quantum free particle, has a wave function that is identical in form to the harmonic functions that characterize the asymptotic dynamics of conscious agents; particles are vibrations not of strings but of interacting conscious agents. This allows us to reinterpret physical properties such as position, momentum, and energy as properties of interacting conscious agents, rather than as preexisting physical truths. We sketch how this approach might extend to the perception of relativistic quantum objects, and to classical objects of macroscopic scale.

#tbt - this is me (ian) in 2008.  i was 21 and just started working parties in LA with a company called @thedfm.  i had to do all the crummy jobs; running drinks, getting people at the door, film on a handheld (or flip cam for those that remember). i stayed in that scene for about 6 years, slowly working my way up - - going from intern to part time, part time to full time.  i never really made any real money, enough to get by and that was fine.  but more important than that was what i got to be apart of.  I worked on mix tapes with artists like big sean, i got to open a pop-up store in echo park, i went to sxsw every year and booked everyone from raekwon and tinashe to hudson mohawke and theophilus london.  i got to develop my taste and my style through these years of grinding; Iâ€™m thankful everyday for getting to do bixel boys today, but i know it would have never have materialized without paying my dues.
